   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "There are missing values in workclass, occupation, and native country. There do no seem to be missing values (N/A) for the quantitative columns. Exactly how many total rows are there where there is missing information?"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 5,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "def find_indices_with_value(df, value):\n",
    "    \"\"\"Return the row indices of a Pandas Dataframe where the row contains the given value.\n",
    "    \n",
    "    Parameters\n",
    "    ----------\n",
    "    \n",
    "    df: Pandas Dataframe\n",
    "    value: value we want to see if row contains\n",
    "    \n",
    "    Return\n",
    "    ------\n",
    "    array\n",
    "        An integer array where each value is the row index of a row that contains the value\n",
    "        \n",
    "    Example\n",
    "    -------\n",
    "    \n",
    "    >>> row0 = [\">\", \"?\", \"!\"]\n",
    "    ... df = pd.DataFrame([row0])\n",
    "    ... find_indices_with_value(df, \"?\")\n",
    "    array([0])\n",
    "    \"\"\"    \n",
    "    \n",
    "    rows = []\n",
    "    for index, row in df.iterrows():\n",
    "        if value in row.unique():\n",
    "            rows.append(index)\n",
    "    return np.array(rows)"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "Note: We saved this function to a .py file for later notebook uses just through copying and pasting. We could not find a way to automatically save this function as a .py file to facilitate reproducibility, but maybe it exists!"
   ]
  },

    }
   ],
   "source": [
    "missing_ind = find_indices_with_value(adult, \"?\")\n",
    "len(missing_ind)"
   ]

    "fig.savefig(\"fig/columns.png\")"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "There are a couple of interesting observations: \n",
    "* The distribution of ages is skewed to the right, which should not surprise us since as individuals get older, they leave the labor force. \n",
    "* The years of educations since 4th grade seem to have 2 peaks, one at 9 and one at 13. 9 years of education since 4th grade means the individual has graduated high school, while 13 years of education since 4th grade means the individual has graduated college. It is no surprise that most people in this dataset have a high school education or higher. \n",
    "* About 50% of the individuals in the dataset are married.\n",
    "* About 85% of the individuals in the dataset identified as White. This likely include Hispanics too. \n",
    "* About 2/3 of the individuals in the dataset were male, while 1/3 of the individuals in the dataset were female. Since it was the 1994, the female labor participation was still pretty low. Now around 47 percent of the labor force is female."
   ]
  },

    "        row1 = [\"3\", \"1\", \"?\"]\n",
